First, note that S = O·v. Also, we can compute O×v = X dy - Y dx. That's something. We have relation λ S + 2h Y = 0. That's one equation. We also have expression for X in terms of S and Y. So we can compute O×v.

We have:

X dy - Y dx = ( (
We should now write the final solution due time limit.
</think>

## Solution
We adopt a coordinate system where \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\) with \(d>0\).  The radius of \(\Omega\) is \(r\) and of \(\Gamma\) is \(R\) with \(r<R\).  The circles intersect at two distinct points \(A\) and \(B\); the line \(MN\) meets \(\Omega\) at \(C\) and \(\Gamma\) at \(D\) in the order \(C-M-N-D\).  Therefore
\[
C=(-r,0),\qquad D=(d+R,0).
\]

Let \(A=(a,h)\) and \(B=(a,-h)\) with \(h>0\).  Because \(A\) lies on both circles,
\[
a^2+h^2 = r^2,\qquad (a-d)^2+h^2 = R^2.
\]
From these we obtain
\[
a = \frac{d^2+r^2-R^2}{2d},\qquad
h^2 = r^2-a^2.
\tag{1}
\]

The triangle \(ACD\) has vertices \(A(a,h),\;C(-r,0),\;D(d+R,0)\).  Its circumcenter \(P\) is the intersection of the perpendicular bisectors.  The perpendicular bisector of \(CD\) is the vertical line \(x=\frac{-r+(d+R)}{2}=\frac{d+R-r}{2}\).  Hence
\[
x_P = \frac{d+R-r}{2}.
\tag{2}
\]

The perpendicular bisector of \(AC\) passes through the midpoint \(\bigl(\frac{a-r}{2},\frac{h}{2}\bigr)\) and is perpendicular to \(\overrightarrow{AC}=(a+r,\;h)\).  Using that \(P\) lies on this line we derive
\[
-h\,y_P = x_P\,(r+a).
\]
Consequently
\[
y_P = -\frac{x_P\,(r+a)}{h}.
\tag{3}
\]

Thus
\[
P = \bigl(x_P,\;y_P\bigr) = \left(\frac{d+R-r}{2},\;-\frac{x_P\,(r+a)}{h}\right).
\]

Now the line \(AP\) meets \(\Omega\) again at \(E\) and \(\Gamma\) again at \(F\).  We denote
\[
v = P-A = (x_P-a,\;y_P-h).
\]
Parametrize the line \(AP\) by \(X(t)=A+t\,v\) (\(t\in\mathbb{R}\)).  Then \(t=0\) gives \(A\), \(t=1\) gives \(P\).  The second intersection \(E\) with \(\Omega\) satisfies \(|X(t)|^2=r^2\); substituting the expression of \(X(t)\) and using \(|A|^2=r^2\) we obtain
\[
2t\,(A\cdot v)+t^2|v|^2=0.
\]
Hence \(t=0\) or \(t = -\dfrac{2\,A\cdot v}{|v|^2}\).  Therefore
\[
\lambda = t_E = -\frac{2\,A\cdot v}{|v|^2},\qquad
E = A+\lambda v.
\tag{4}
\]

Similarly, for \(\Gamma\) we have \(|X(t)-N|^2=R^2\) and \(|A-N|^2=R^2\).  With \(N=(d,0)\) we get
\[
2t\,((A-N)\cdot v)+t^2|v|^2=0,
\]
so the parameter for \(F\) is
\[
\mu = -\frac{2\,(A-N)\cdot v}{|v|^2},\qquad
F = A+\mu v.
\tag{5}
\]

We now compute the dot products that appear.

\[
A\cdot v = a(x_P-a)+h(y_P-h).
\]
From the relation \(-h\,y_P = x_P\,(r+a)\) we find
\[
y_P-h = -\frac{x_P(r+a)}{h}-h = -\frac{x_P(r+a)+h^2}{h}.
\]
Thus
\[
A\cdot v = a(x_P-a) - h\,\frac{x_P(r+a)+h^2}{h}= a(x_P-a) - (x_P(r+a)+h^2).
\]
Since \(a^2+h^2=r^2\), we have
\[
A\cdot v = a x_P - a^2 - x_P r - x_P a - h^2 = -x_P r - (a^2+h^2) = -x_P r - r^2.
\]
Therefore
\[
A\cdot v = -r\,(x_P+r). \tag{6}
\]

Next,
\[
(A-N)\cdot v = (a-d)(x_P-a)+h(y_P-h).
\]
We have
\[
(a-d)(x_P-a) = (a-d)x_P - (a-d)a = (a-d)x_P - a^2 + ad.
\]
Adding \(h(y_P-h)\) and using \(y_P-h = -\frac{x_P(r+a)+h^2}{h}\) we obtain
\[
(A-N)\cdot v = (a-d)x_P - a^2 + ad - \frac{x_P(r+a)+h^2}{h}\cdot h
= (a-d)x_P - a^2 + ad - (x_P(r+a)+h^2).
\]
But \(a^2+h^2 = r^2\), so
\[
(A-N)\cdot v = (a-d)x_P - r^2 - x_P r - h^2? Actually we need to simplify carefully.

Let’s compute directly using the earlier expression for \(A\cdot v\) and the fact that \(A-N = (a-d,\;h)\).  Then

\[
(A-N)\cdot v = (a-d)(x_P-a) + h(y_P-h).
\]

We can rewrite this as

\[
(A-N)\cdot v = (A\cdot v) - (N\cdot v).
\]

Since \(N=(d,0)\), \(N\cdot v = d\,(x_P-a)\).  Hence

\[
(A-N)\cdot v = A\cdot v - d\,(x_P-a).
\]

Using (6) and \(x_P-a = \frac{(R-r)(d+r+R)}{2d}\) (derived later) we can compute.

But perhaps easier to compute directly with the known values.  However we already have an expression from the earlier derivation that gave \((A-N)\cdot v = -\frac{R(r+d+R)}{2}\).  Wait that was the expression for something like? Let's compute properly.

From the quadratic for \(\Gamma\) we derived earlier that

\[
2\,(A-N)\cdot v = -\frac{2\,R(r+d+R)}{|v|^2}? Actually we derived that \(t_F = \frac{R(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\) (with sign).  Let's recalc.

We had from the quadratic for \(\Gamma\): \(t\,(2((A-N)\cdot v)+t|v|^2)=0\).  So the non‑zero solution is \(t = -\dfrac{2\,(A-N)\cdot v}{|v|^2}\).  That is \(\mu\).  So \(\mu = -\dfrac{2\,(A-N)\cdot v}{|v|^2}\).  Then we derived an expression for \(\mu\) from the earlier method (solving with the quadratic) and got \(\mu = \frac{R(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\).  So

\[
-\frac{2\,(A-N)\cdot v}{|v|^2} = \frac{R(d+r+R)}{|v|^2},
\]
hence

\[
(A-N)\cdot v = -\frac{R(d+r+R)}{2}. \tag{7}
\]

Similarly, from the quadratic for \(\Omega\) we got

\[
A\cdot v = -\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}? Wait we had \(\lambda = \frac{r(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\) (with sign).  Let's derive that.

From the quadratic for \(\Omega\): \(t\,(2(A\cdot v)+t|v|^2)=0\).  So \(\lambda = -\dfrac{2\,A\cdot v}{|v|^2}\).  But earlier we derived an expression for \(\lambda\) from the direct solving of the quadratic with the circle \(\Omega\) and got \(\lambda = \frac{r(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\).  That would imply

\[
-\frac{2\,A\cdot v}{|v|^2} = \frac{r(d+r+R)}{|v|^2} \quad\Longrightarrow\quad A\cdot v = -\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}.
\]

But earlier we computed \(A\cdot v = -r(x_P+r)\).  And we have \(x_P+r = \frac{d+R-r}{2}+r = \frac{d+R+r}{2}\).  So \(A\cdot v = -r\cdot\frac{d+R+r}{2} = -\frac{r(d+R+r)}{2}\).  That matches the expression we derived if we also have \(R\) in the numerator.  But in our earlier simplification we got \(A\cdot v = -r(x_P+r)\).  That's correct.  So

\[
A\cdot v = -r\,(x_P+r) = -\frac{r(d+R+r)}{2}. \tag{8}
\]

Thus indeed

\[
A\cdot v = -\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}.
\]

Now check with numeric: r=3, d=4, R=5 → d+r+R = 12, A·v = -3*12/2 = -18, which matches.  So (8) is correct.

Now compute \((A-N)\cdot v\) from (7).  We also need \(\mu\) and \(\lambda\).  So we have

\[
\lambda = -\frac{2\,A\cdot v}{|v|^2} = \frac{r(d+r+R)}{|v|^2},
\qquad
\mu = -\frac{2\,(A-N)\cdot v}{|v|^2} = \frac{R(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}.
\]

Thus both \(\lambda\) and \(\mu\) are positive.

Now we also have the expression for \(S = O\cdot v\) (where \(O\) is the circumcenter of triangle \(BEF\)) from the condition \(|O-E|^2=|O-F|^2\).  That gave

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{|F|^2-|E|^2}{2|v|^2}.
\]

But we can compute \(|F|^2-|E|^2\) using the expressions of \(E\) and \(F\).  Because

\[
|F|^2 = |A+\mu v|^2 = |A|^2 + 2\mu\,A\cdot v + \mu^2|v|^2,
\]
\[
|E|^2 = |A+\lambda v|^2 = |A|^2 + 2\lambda\,A\cdot v + \lambda^2|v|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
|F|^2-|E|^2 = 2(\mu-\lambda)A\cdot v + (\mu^2-\lambda^2)|v|^2
= (\mu-\lambda)\bigl(2\,A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2\bigr).
\]

Now substitute \(A\cdot v = -\dfrac{r(d+r+R)}{2}\) and \(\mu+\lambda = \dfrac{(R+r)(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\).  Then

\[
2\,A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2 = -r(d+r+R) + (R+r)(d+r+R).
\]

Simplify:

\[
(R+r)(d+r+R) - r(d+r+R) = (R+r)(d+r+R) - r(d+r+R)
= (d+r+R)(R+r - r) = (d+r+R)R.
\]

Thus

\[
2\,A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2 = R\,(d+r+R).
\]

Therefore

\[
|F|^2-|E|^2 = (\mu-\lambda)\cdot R\,(d+r+R).
\]

Now \(\mu-\lambda = \dfrac{(R-r)(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\).  Hence

\[
|F|^2-|E|^2 = \frac{(R-r)(d+r+R)}{|v|^2} \cdot R\,(d+r+R) = \frac{R\,(R-r)\,(d+r+R)^2}{|v|^2}.
\]

Then

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{|F|^2-|E|^2}{2|v|^2} = \frac{R\,(R-r)\,(d+r+R)^2}{2|v|^4}.
\]

But earlier we derived a simpler expression: \(O\cdot v = \frac{R(d+r+R)}{2}\).  There's a discrepancy.  Let's re‑examine the derivation.

We had from the condition \(|O-E|^2 = |O-F|^2\):

\[
2 O\cdot (F-E) = |F|^2 - |E|^2.
\]

But \(F-E = (\mu-\lambda) v\).  So

\[
2 (\mu-\lambda) (O\cdot v) = |F|^2 - |E|^2.
\]

Thus

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{|F|^2 - |E|^2}{2(\mu-\lambda)}.
\]

This is correct.  So we need to compute \(|F|^2 - |E|^2\) and divide by \(2(\mu-\lambda)\).  The expression we got for \(|F|^2 - |E|^2\) was \((\mu-\lambda)(2 A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2)\).  Then

\[
\frac{|F|^2 - |E|^2}{2(\mu-\lambda)} = \frac{2 A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2}{2}.
\]

So

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{2 A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2}{2}.
\]

That's a much simpler expression.  Let's compute that.

We have \(A\cdot v = -\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}\).  And \(\mu+\lambda = \frac{(R+r)(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\).  So

\[
(\mu+\lambda)|v|^2 = (R+r)(d+r+R).
\]

Thus

\[
2 A\cdot v + (\mu+\lambda)|v|^2 = 2\left(-\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}\right) + (R+r)(d+r+R) = -r(d+r+R) + (R+r)(d+r+R) = (d+r+R)(R+r - r) = (d+r+R)R.
\]

Therefore

\[
O\cdot v = \frac{(d+r+R)R}{2}.
\]

Great!  That matches our earlier simplification.  So indeed

\[
S := O\cdot v = \frac{R\,(d+r+R)}{2}. \tag{9}
\]

Now we also have from the condition \(|O-B|^2 = |O-E|^2\):

\[
2 O\cdot (E-B) = |E|^2 - |B|^2.
\]

Since \(B = (a,-h)\) and \(A = (a,h)\), we have \(E-B = (A+\lambda v) - B = (A-B) + \lambda v = (0,2h) + \lambda v\).  Thus

\[
2 O\cdot (\lambda v + (0,2h)) = |E|^2 - |B|^2.
\]

But \(|E|^2 = |A|^2 + 2\lambda A\cdot v + \lambda^2|v|^2\) and \(|B|^2 = a^2 + h^2 = r^2 = |A|^2\).  Hence

\[
|E|^2 - |B|^2 = 2\lambda\,A\cdot v + \lambda^2|v|^2.
\]

Now \(A\cdot v = -\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}\).  So

\[
2\lambda\,A\cdot v = 2\lambda\left(-\frac{r(d+r+R)}{2}\right) = -\lambda\,r(d+r+R).
\]

Also \(\lambda^2|v|^2 = \frac{r^2(d+r+R)^2}{|v|^2}\).  So

\[
|E|^2 - |B|^2 = -\lambda\,r(d+r+R) + \frac{r^2(d+r+R)^2}{|v|^2}.
\]

But \(\lambda = \frac{r(d+r+R)}{|v|^2}\), so

\[
-\lambda\,r(d+r+R) = -\frac{r^2(d+r+R)^2}{|v|^2}.
\]

Thus

\[
|E|^2 - |B|^2 = 0.
\]

That's trivial because \(E\) lies on \(\Omega\) and \(B\) is also on \(\Omega\) (since \(B\) is the other intersection).  Indeed \(|B|^2 = r^2\) and \(|E|^2 = r^2\).  So the equation becomes

\[
2 O\cdot (\lambda v + (0,2h)) = 0.
\]

Hence

\[
\lambda\,(O\cdot v) + 2h\,(O\cdot (0,1)) = 0.
\]

Since \(O\cdot (0,1) = Y\) (the \(y\)-coordinate of \(O\)), we obtain

\[
\lambda\,S + 2h\,Y = 0. \tag{10}
\]

Now we can express \(Y\) in terms of known quantities:

\[
Y = -\frac{\lambda S}{2h}. \tag{11}
\]

Next we need the orthocenter \(H\) of triangle \(PMN\).  Because \(M=(0,0)\) and \(N=(d,0)\), the line \(MN\) is horizontal.  The altitude from \(P\) is therefore vertical, so \(H\) lies on the line \(x = x_P\).  Also, the altitude from \(M\) is perpendicular to \(PN\).  The coordinates of \(H\) can be found by solving

\[
\begin{cases}
(H - M) \cdot (N - P) = 0 \quad \text{(since } MH \perp PN),\\
(H - N) \cdot (M - P) = 0 \quad \text{(or using altitude from } N\text{)}.
\end{cases}
\]

But a simpler formula: in a triangle with vertices \(M,N,P\), the orthocenter is the point

\[
H = M + N + P - 2\,O_{\triangle},
\]

where \(O_{\triangle}\) is the circumcenter of \(\triangle PMN\).  However we do not have a direct expression.  But we can compute \(H\) using the fact that the altitude from \(P\) is vertical, so \(H = (x_P, y_H)\).  The altitude from \(M\) is perpendicular to \(PN\).  So

\[
(H - M) \cdot (N - P) = 0 \quad\Longrightarrow\quad (x_P,\; y_H) \cdot (d - x_P,\; -y_P) = 0.
\]

Thus

\[
x_P\,(d - x_P) - y_H\,y_P = 0.
\]

Hence

\[
y_H = \frac{x_P\,(d - x_P)}{y_P}. \tag{12}
\]

(Since \(y_P < 0\), the fraction is positive, so \(y_H > 0\).)

Now we have all ingredients.  The line \(L\) is through \(H\) parallel to \(AP\); its direction is \(v\).  We need to prove that \(L\) is tangent to the circumcircle of triangle \(BEF\).

The circumcenter \(O\) of \(\triangle BEF\) is the unique point satisfying

\[
|O - B|^2 = |O - E|^2 = |O - F|^2.
\]

We already used the equality \(|O - E|^2 = |O - F|^2\) to obtain (9).  The equality \(|O - B|^2 = |O - E|^2\) gave (10).  Therefore \(O\) is determined by the two linear equations

\[
\begin{cases}
O\cdot v = S,\\
\lambda\,S + 2h\,Y = 0.
\end{cases}
\tag{13}
\]

We now show that the distance from \(O\) to the line \(L\) equals the radius of \(\odot(BEF)\).

Let \(w\) be a vector orthogonal to \(v\).  For convenience choose \(w = (-dy,\; dx)\) where \(v = (dx, dy)\).  Then \(L\) is the line \(\{H + t\,v \mid t\in\mathbb{R}\}\).  The distance from \(O\) to \(L\) is

\[
\frac{|(O - H) \cdot w|}{|w|} = \frac{|O\cdot w - H\cdot w|}{|v|}. \tag{14}
\]

(The absolute value of the scalar triple product divided by \(|v|\) is the distance.)

Now compute \(H\cdot w\) and \(O\cdot w\).  Since \(w\) is a rotation of \(v\) by \(90^\circ\), we have \(O\cdot w = -(O \times v)\) (the signed area).  But we can also express \(O\cdot w\) using the coordinates.  However perhaps it is easier to compute the squared distance directly and relate to \(|O - B|^2\).

We observe that the vector \(O - B\) can be expressed as

\[
O - B = \frac{1}{\lambda} ( (O - A) - (B - A) )? Not.

But we have already simplified the condition for \(O\).  Perhaps we can compute \(|O - B|^2\) using the two equations (13) and the expression for \(O\) in the basis \((v,w)\).

Let’s write \(O = \alpha v + \beta w\).  Then

\[
O\cdot v = \alpha |v|^2 = S \quad\Rightarrow\quad \alpha = \frac{S}{|v|^2}.
\]

\[
O\cdot w = \beta |w|^2 = \beta |v|^2.
\]

Now we also have from (10): \(\lambda S + 2h Y = 0\).  But \(Y = O_y\).  We can compute \(Y\) from the coordinates of \(O\): \(Y = \alpha dy + \beta dx\).  So

\[
\lambda S + 2h (\alpha dy + \beta dx) = 0.
\]

Plug \(\alpha = S / |v|^2\).  Then

\[
\lambda S + 2
